Summary

On a random, depressing day, in a bar the brokenhearted professor Rio Vidal knows all too well, she sees a woman—or, as she describes her in her head, an ethereal being, the painter Agatha Harkness.

A woman whose mere presence sobered Rio up, then made her drunk again for an entirely different reason.

Can Rio—a woman who doubts her self-worth, who believes she's undeserving of love—handle holding the door open for someone as delicate and willing as Agatha?
And if she does, can she handle letting her in afterward?

Rio arrived at work on time, this was the first time in months. She woke up feeling great, nothing bothered her all morning, not even herself.

She was sitting in her office, doing some work she should have completed months ago. Then her mind drifted back to Agatha. The way they felt so close to each other yet too far away. Rio couldn't really understand this strange connection she felt that linked her to Agatha, or why it even exists. At the party two days ago, she momentarily thought Agatha would give her her number, or mention something, or even ask Rio for hers. But Agatha disappeared after a while, and Rio wasn't even able to look at her eyes one last time.

Her fingers hovered over the keyboard, typing Agatha Harkness' name absentmindedly.

Results appeared once Rio clicked "enter": photos of the woman, limited information, and her artworks.

She looked at the woman, admiring her sharp features and how she looked perfect in every photo.

Rio Read the information that the internet allowed her to access, but there wasn't much—just some articles that barely contained anything.

Rio scrolled down, viewing the artworks, there were dozens of them. Each one looks like it possesses a piece of Agatha. They looked like her. Rio wasn't practically invested in paintings, but she could see and feel how every painting screamed Agatha's name—her art style, the colors she uses, the details.

Rio examined each painting closely, trying to figure out how and why each one was Agatha.

She noticed the number of portraits of women and the naked bodies. Some paintings felt intimate, filled with emotions—the angles, the poses, the women in the paintings. Rio found herself wondering if those women were Agatha's partners or her muses, and what they meant to her.

Then she looked and saw the painting Alice had in her office. She had always loved that painting and felt a connection to it, something she couldn't quite name but still felt.

The picture contained three colors: black, red and a dark shade of gray. It's not obvious what the picture truly represents, what it's about, or why it filled Rio's heart with a sense of remorse every time she looked at it. This one doesn't resemble any painting of Agatha's, it's strangely different, it holds something within its strictly limited details, and Rio was curious to discover what is so special about this piece, why it felt personal . She tried to collect the information she had found but it was merely useless.

The workday had come to an end, Rio gathered her things and stepped outside the office, meeting Alice in the hallway.

“Hey, you” Alice greeted with a smile

“Hey,” Rio replied, mirroring Alice's smile.

They walked in silence for a few minutes until Rio broke it.

“Um, so, I wanted to ask you about something,”

Alice looked at her to continue.

“About that painting in your office—Agatha's.”

“What about it?”

“What do you know about it?”

“Not much really. I bought it years ago, because when I looked at it for the first time, I felt like I should have it. The only thing I know is that it's one of Agatha's earliest works, from when she was in college. She hadn't painted much at the time, yet she refused to show her work to the public—epecially this one. But years after her graduation she started publishing her work. I don't really know what it's about; I don't think that I actually understand the true meaning behind the painting, but it kept growing in me.”

“Oh” was the only response Rio could master.

“Yeah, you should ask Lilia, she definitely knows something—if not everything.”

Then seconds of silence enveloped them.

“What were you two talking about, anyway?” Alice asked.

“Who?”

“You and Agatha.”

“Oh, nothing really,” Rio paused. “Lilia introduced me to her.”

“Yeah? Because, I think that woman was looking at you—like really looking at you.” Alice said, enjoyment filling her tone.

Rio stared into space, thinking about what Alice's aiming at. Moments of silence followed her words as they reached the parking lot.

“How do you mean?” Rio asked after a while.

“I don't know, but I felt something there.”

“Ali, you're delusional.” Rio replied and got into her car without looking back at Alice.

“We'll see about that! See you!” Alice was practically screaming at that point.

Rio only laughed and started the engine, pretending that Alice's conclusions did not matter.

She didn't go home; instead she stayed outside the walls of her empty, depressing house.

She gifted herself a proper meal, considering it a self–date, because she needed that and she had already begun forgetting what real food actually tasted like.

Once at home, she collapsed onto the couch after taking off her shoes and jacket. The dimly lit living room was forcing Rio to close her eyes but after a brief second she forced them open. “No, not today Rio.”

Then she stood on her feet and headed to the bathroom, taking the quiet, warm bath that she deserves.

She wrapped herself in a towel, went back to her bedroom and grabbed the same oversized t–shirt that she always found comfort in wearing.

She sat on the bed, “What should I do now?”

Nothing was in her head to waste the remaining time of the day. She thought about calling Alice and going out for some drinks but it was too early for that, instead she called Lilia.

“Hello?” There was some noise in Lilia's side.

“Hey, kid. Nice hearing your voice.”

Rio laughed. “Are you busy?”

“Not really, do you want something?”

“Well, I thought, do you want to go out?”

“Yeah sure why not. Are you hungry?”

“No, not really”

“Okay then, just give me an hour.”

“Alright.”

So she got up, put on some clothes: a t–shirt, a jacket, and trousers, did her hair, applied her makeup on, and went out.

She drove to the café where she was supposed to meet Lilia, and she was already there.

They hugged once Rio approached her, then she sat, facing her.

“How are you doing?” Lilia asked

“Fine, good. What about you?”

“Great. Here, I got you your coffee.”

“Thanks. And yours?”

“Nope, no caffeine for me darling.”

They talked for a while, talking about their lives recently though there wasn't much to talk about really.

“I wanted to ask you something.”

Lilia looked at her “Go on.”

“About that painting of Agatha Harkness, Black: My True Love's Hear t.”

“What about it?”

“I don't know. I just feel something when I look at it, something strange. I asked Alice about it today but she didn't know much about it.” Rio paused, took a sip from her cup. “She said you probably know something.”

“I maybe do. Well, the painting is really personal to Agatha. When I asked her about it when we first met years ago, her facial expressions changed upon mentioning it. She said the painting was never meant to be left exposed to the public's eyes and opinions, but she was in deep need of money. She didn't talk about the process of painting it or what it means, but she said it's her most spiritual work, and it defines her the most.”

Rio listened to Lilia carefully, afraid of missing a detail.

“Is she always that mysterious?”

“Yes, always. She doesn't let anybody in. And her intensity makes her the great artist that she is. Honestly, she's one of the greatest artists I've ever worked with.”

Well, now Rio is left with no answers but more questions, and she needed something to quell her curiosity.

They talked for a while about nothing and everything all at once.

“Now, you should take me home.”

“You didn't come in your car?”

“No, I took a cab, but since you're here, I'm depending on you.”

“So, you're taking advantage of me?”

“Exactly, but I'll cook you dinner.”

“Well, I like that.”

Rio chuckled and got up from her chair, and Lilia followed her movements.

Once Rio stopped the car in front of Lilia's house, Lilia said, “Agatha is staying with me for a few days until she finds the apartment that she wants, she...”

“Jesus, Lilia, why are you telling me this now?” Rio said, absolutely stunned.

“What? I didn't think it would be a problem,”

Rio sighed, “It's not, but you could have told me before.”

“I forgot,”

“No, you didn't. You want me to meet her, again.”

“Shut up, Sherlock.” Lilia said as she took off her seatbelt. “Anyway, she doesn't live in Los Angeles; she settles in Paris, so she's staying with me for now,” Lilia said and got out of the car.

Rio was absolutely shocked because, damn.

Lilia knocked on the window telling Rio to get out, and so she did.

Lilia opened the door and motioned for Rio to step inside. She was nervous, an anxiety rush traveled through her entire body and settled in her stomach.

They got in and Rio sat on the couch, there was no sign of Agatha, which was good—now she could breathe.

“Do you want something to drink dear?” Lilia called from the kitchen

Rio got up and followed her there.

“Oh God, yes please!”

“Here,” Lilia said as she handed her a glass of red wine.

They returned to the living room and sat opposite each other. They were talking about something but Rio's mind couldn't really focus on the conversation, she's thinking about Agatha who still hadn't shown any sign of showing up.

“Are you alright?” Lilia asked with a concerned tone.

“Yeah. Yeah, totally—I just zoned out.”

Then the door swung open. Agatha.

Rio's eyes immediately found hers once she turned around, and Agatha did the same thing. Seeing Rio, a stunned expression overtook her face for a brief second, but she quickly replaced it with a smile, and Rio noticed that, how could she not?

“I just went out to buy something,” Agatha said, speaking with Lilia while looking at Rio.

“Well, Rio here is staying for dinner,” Lilia said also looking at Rio, too much gazing on her direction.

Rio realized that she was also staring, so she sprang to her feet, took a few steps toward Agatha, and extended her hand. Agatha shook it gladly,

“Nice seeing you again, Rio.” Agatha said. This time she wasn't tasting the sound of her name, she was devouring it with great pleasure.

“Likewise,” Rio replied, then withdraw her hand from Agatha's and sat back down on the couch.

“Excuse me for a few minutes ladies,” Agatha said, glancing at Lilia and then back at Rio.

“Take your time darling,” Lilia replied.

Then Agatha walked away toward what Rio assumed was her room in Lilia's house.

And 6 minutes later, she returned, Rio counted the seconds. Of course she did.

Agatha was wearing an oversized earthy green button–up shirt and black sweatpants. Rio found herself looking at her and Agatha seemed to notice that too.

She looked like she was considering the options, whether to sit beside Rio or Lilia, she ended up choosing Lilia's side.

“What do you girls want for dinner?” Lilia asked, looking at them both.

“Anything really,” Rio replied.

“The Chicken Florentine Pasta that you made the other day? I can still taste it, so I'd very much love to eat it again!” Agatha said enthusiastically while looking at Lilia.

“Great, easy and delicious.” Lilia said in approval.

Rio then looked at Lilia, then her gaze drifted to Agatha and the open buttons of her shirt, and of course Agatha noticed. She threw an unreadable smirk toward Rio. So Rio tried to busy herself with the last sip of wine that was left in her glass.

A minute later, Agatha got up, went to the kitchen, and came back with two glasses filled with wine. Agatha approached Rio and handed her a glass then took the empty one and set it aside. She looked at Rio then clinked her glass to hers.

“Cheers.”

“Cheers.”

They both looked at each other as they took their first sip, brown met blue and assorted with it for a fleeting moment, then Agatha looked away and sat back down on the couch.

Lilia broke the silence that embraced the three of them “Alright girls, I'm going to make us dinner, you rest here,” and with that she left, leaving Rio alone with Agatha.

The silence that embraced them seconds ago now started to choke Rio, but Agatha loosened its grip on Rio's throat with that sweet voice of hers, rich with depth. A one–word question.

“How?”

Rio looked at her, confused.

“What?”

“You said at the party that what I do suits me. I asked you 'how?' but I didn't get the chance to hear your answer.” Agatha said with a smirk, then took a sip from her glass.

Does this woman always start her conversations with such intensity?

“Yeah because you left .” Rio thought to herself, but of course she didn't say that, that was a forbidden territory.

“You've got an incredible memory.” Rio said with a chuckle.

“One of my blessings.”

Rio's mind paused longer than necessary, she can't think of anything.

“So, how?”

“It's just, you know, it suits you. I can't really imagine you being in a normal job or anything else.” a pause. “Being an artist I mean, it suits you. You, you look artistic. I mean, yeah, like a painting.” The words slipped from her tongue and it's to late. That should have stayed in her head. Rio realized the words that came out of her mouth and drank what was left in her glass, which was the whole glass.

“Easy there.” Agatha said, looking at Rio with intensity and something more—so much more.

The empty glass now resting in her hand. Looking back at Agatha, their eyes locked and neither of them looked away, as if they both were daring each other, testing the waters.

Rio felt herself stuck here. In this place. With this woman. Part of her wants to stay because it feels so good to be stuck with her. But she also isn't able to handle it, to handle all those unexplainable things—the floating emotions, and the charged atmosphere. The way Agatha is looking at her, the woman's eyes are seductive—an ocean of blue that Rio is willing to be drowned in.

“I'm gonna see if Lilia needs anything.”

An escape.

With that, she left her spot on the couch and walked toward the kitchen, she could still feel Agatha's eyes on her.

“Do you need anything?” Rio asked, still feeling awkward.

Lilia looked at her, “No darling, I told you to rest.”

“I don't really need to.” Rio paused, “I'm gonna be outside for a minute.”

“Are you alright?”

“Yeah, no, I'm fine, I just need a smoke.”

“Rio Vidal, when did you start smoking again?”

“Five days ago, Lilia Calderu.”

“Kid, don't do that to yourself!” Lilia said, pointing a spoon at her.

“Okay” Rio said with a chuckle as she left the kitchen. She heard Lilia's sigh

She was heading to the front door when a voice made her stop,

“Going somewhere?”

“Um, no, I just need a cigarette.”

“Do you mind if I join you?”

“Of course not.”

They smoked in silence, the sound of burning paper filling their ears. The chill breeze added a layer of intensity. They both wanted to say something to break the silence, but neither did. They only looked at each other, their eyes filled with intensity, unspoken words, and a hanging promise

When they went back inside, Lilia saw them, like if she had caught some kids sneaking out,

“I just want to know why people don't care about their health.”

Agatha looked at Rio and they both laughed without responding.

They were all chatting in the kitchen, helping Lilia, talking about things. Rio found it easy to talk with Agatha if someone else was there with them, things felt less awkward and Rio could find her own voice. But every time their eyes met, Rio remained silent, no matter what the topic was or what they were talking about, and it also didn't matter if she was in the middle of a sentence.

Rio was saying something about some college students when her eyes met Agatha's, and Rio became quiet all of a sudden. It felt as if Agatha's eyes were a maze and she was lost in them, unable to find the entrance or the exit.

“Rio, are you alright?” Lilia's voice brought her back,

“Yeah, absolutely.” She paused, and took the plates. “I'm gonna take these.”

She placed them on the table, took a deep breathe then turned around to go back to the kitchen.

“Are you okay?” This time it was Agatha. Agatha's voice. Agatha's presence.

“Yeah, just a, um, just a headache.”

“Yeah?”

“Yeah.”

Lilia came to join them with a bottle of wine in her hand.

They sat, and of course Agatha would sit facing her; of course she would.

“This is so good, Lilia,” Rio said

“Exactly! It's so good.” Agatha said in affirmation.

They ate while talking about things here and there, Rio felt good here, between these two.

by the third glass of wine, Rio was completely drunk.

Lilia left to do something—Rio didn't really know what. She wasn't paying attention.

“Why are you staring at me?” Rio asked, almost a whisper.

“I'm not staring at you.” Agatha said in her normal tone.

“No, you are. You're staring at me.” Rio insisted, still whispering.

“And what If I'm really staring at you? Is it a problem?” Agatha replied, matching Rio's tone. She waited for Rio's response with a smirk on her face.

“Yes,” Rio said after a few seconds.

Agatha raised an eyebrow at that, and the smirk never left her face. “Yeah? And what is it?”

“It makes me drunk, the way you stare at me... I mean, yeah, this is, um, this is my fifth glass, but um, but it's different. It's not the alcohol,” Rio said while leaning in the chair.

“You're adorable, you know that?”

Oh, Agatha was also drunk.

“Yes, I know” Rio said, grinning and Agatha laughed at that. She really is adorable.

“I like your painting.”

“Yeah? Which one.”

“The one that makes me feel guilty and sad.”

“Guilty and sad? Which one is that?”

“I don't know Agatha,”

Agatha's eyes widened upon hearing her name from Rio for the first time.

“Tell me which one when we're both sober.” She said after a second.

“Will do ma'am”

Agatha smiled.

By the time Lilia came back they were wasted. She tried to make Rio stay the night but Rio refused, so Lilia called a cab for her.

Rio grabbed her jacket and stepped outside; it was a cold night.

“Hey, give me your phone.”

A voice from behind made her open her eyes. She turned around and handed her phone to Agatha.

Agatha put down her number, “There, just in case.”

In case of what?

Rio smiled at her, and got into the cab, going home.

Chapter End Notes

Tbh, I feel like I'm mischaracterizing everyone

Chapter Four

Chapter Notes

Hey guys!
I want to say something.
I'm not really used to writing slow burns, and I'm not actually used to writing anything, but I need to get this idea out of my system.
Well, English isn't my first language so I have to re–read the chapters until I'm sick of them, and everytime I re–read one, I find a mistake or a misspelling, and that makes me feel really weird, but I'd appreciate it if you guys could just ignore them, please bear with me. Also, I don't know where this is going, but I hope I can write what I have in my head and describe it properly, but trust me we'll get there.

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Rio stared at the ringing phone. She had called five times already, and it was midnight. The noisy sound disappeared for a few seconds as her phone remained on the table. She took a deep breath and exhaled through her nose. She was furious. Only seconds later, her phone rang again, illuminating the dark room and disturbing the peace.

6 Missed Calls, 3 New Messages

She picked it up.

“What the fuck do you want?”

“Woah, someone's in a bad mood, I see.”

Rio gritted her teeth, her blood was boiling.

“What are you? A child? Do you know what time it is?”

“Oh, I know. I'm also aware that you've never been a good sleeper, so I figured you'd be awake.”

Rio's tongue poked the inside of her cheek. Her left hand clenched into a fist by her side, she was ready to kill someone with her bare hands.

“And you didn't take a hint when I didn't respond? What the fuck do you want, anyway?”

“I need to talk to you.”

“About what? What is there between you and me that we need to talk about? Nothing. Absolutely nothing.”

“Oh come on, Rio. Don't you miss me?”

“I don't. To the point that If I saw your corpse lying on the street, I'd fucking dance on it.”

“Come on baby, don't be like that...”

“I'm not your fucking baby, don't you ever dare call me that. Ever!”

“Okay, okay, just let me talk to you this once,”

“I told you, there's nothing between us to talk about.”

“I know. Just meet me this once—just this time, I want to talk to you.”

“Say it now. What do you want?”

“I want to see you.”

“Oh, fuck you.” Rio said and hung up.

She ran a hand through her dark hair, frustration running through her entire body. She wetted her lips and stood in her place for a while. Then she drank a glass of water in one swig and went to sit on the couch.

“That fucking bitch.” Rio muttered, resting her head between her hands. She always disturbed her peace, always dragged her back to the beginning, always found a way to twist a knife in her back. Always.

Rio looked at the time, just a few hours until sunrise. The evening had gone to waste, and she hadn't gotten a single minute of sleep. It felt like she was trapped in a box—one that fit her perfectly, so tightly that she couldn't even stretch her body, and that box would close and open from time to time, but now, it was shut. No light. No oxygen. Nothing. She couldn't get out. Something—or rather, someone—was choking her for their own pleasure, releasing her throat whenever they pleased. And Rio just couldn't escape, trapped and suffocated.

Morning came, and the sun rose. The sound of birds singing—or maybe cursing, the cold morning breeze, the chatter of people, the world filled with life. It irritated Rio.

Her eyes burned. Her headache was tearing her apart. She had tried to sleep, but her mind hadn't rested for even a second. Right now, her only wish was to sleep and sleep and sleep. Maybe sleep and never wake up again. She feels like shit.

She got up from the couch with a sigh, an exhausted and a heavy one, and dragged her feet upstairs. She stood in the doorway, looking at the bed. God, it looked so comfortable. She couldn't resist it, so she crashed onto the mattress, burying her face in the pillows. Another day, another canceled classes.

She didn't know how many hours had passed when she woke up, confused. She thought she heard a loud knocking at the door. She got up, more irritated than before.

She quickly washed her face, then went downstairs, approaching the front door, she opened it.

And there she was. Who else would disturb and ruin her night and morning but her? No one. Not a single human being.

“What the fuck are you doing at my door? Are you fucking kidding me? Seriously?”

“Hello.”

“Oh fuck off.”

“Just let me in.”

“Are you insane? Seriously, what the fuck is wrong with you? Do you want me to call the police?”

“No, Rio, what’s wrong with you?”

Rio laughed, hard and loud, shaking her head in mock disbelief.

“What’s wrong with me? What’s wrong with me? Are you joking?” She said, unable to believe the irony of the situation

“Let me in. I'm freezing.”

“No, say what you want right here because this is the only chance you get.”

“Fine.” Jane paused. “I'm pregnant.”

“Yeah? I'm sure it's not mine.” Rio said, smirking.

“I wish it was.”

“No, you don't, cut the crap, Jane.”

“I do.” Jane stepped forward, closer to Rio. “I want to raise it with you.”

“Stay right where you are,” Rio said pointing at her ex–girlfriend. “Don't you dare playing this shit with me. You want sympathy? Find it elsewhere.”

“Rio. Please.” Her ex–girlfriend begged, stepping closer and closer.

Rio only looked at her, gritting her teeth.

Jane leaned closer, trying to touch Rio's cheek.

“Go fuck yourself Jane. I don't want to see your face in my life ever again.”

“Your really won't give me an another chance?”

“To do what? Act like a bitch all over again?”

Her ex–girlfriend didn't say a thing.

Rio looked at her, “Leave me alone.” Then she stepped inside, and closed the door.

She leaned her back against it, trying to steady her breathing. “ You did well, Rio. You had to say that. ” She reassured herself through inhales and exhales. Rio didn't glance back at the door to see if her ex–girlfriend was gone or not. It didn't matter.

She went to the kitchen and made herself a cup of coffee, a mixture of feelings running through her, messing with her head. Just yesterday, she was fine—she was great, even—and as if her ex–girlfriend sensed it so she came like a storm to ruin her life all over again.

“Pregnant.” Rio muttered as she took a sip of her coffee. The bitter taste stung her tongue, but it did wonders to calm her head, even if just for a bit.

Most of the day passed. The sun began to set while Rio lay on the couch. She went from one panic attack to an another, and in between, she regretted her entire life—every decision she had ever made. But worst of them all, falling in love with that woman and letting her ruin her, as if she had been blindfolded the entire time.

She forced herself up from the couch after a battle with her own head.

She had to get out from here. This house was holding her captive, making her even more miserable than she already was. She had once lived in love, surrounded by these walls. Now, they mocked her—laughing at how stupid she was. Even the walls knew it.

She wore some clothes without putting much thought into it, she was in her casual state now.

Heading downstairs, she caught sight of the wine bottle resting on the kitchen island. She poured herself a glass, then stared at it. A glass filled with wine.

Agatha handing her a glass, looking at her mysteriously—with mischief and so much more. From now on, red wine means Agatha. Red wine is Agatha. Agatha's eyes. Agatha's smirk. Agatha's intensity. Agatha.

Rio finally took a sip. The acidic taste of the wine lingered on her tongue as she stared at the glass for a few more seconds. Agatha.

Why was that woman in her head? Since when did wine remind her of someone? Since when did she think about someone she knew nothing about? Since when did she miss the way someone looked at her? And the strangest thing of them all—why did she think about Agatha to begin with? Why did she think about her almost everyday since she first saw her?

She studied the glass in her hand, looking at it closely. Then she poured the rest of the wine into her mouth, letting the burning sensation take over her senses for a while.

Rio drove in silence, humming along to the song playing from the car stereo. A cigarette rested between her fingers. She had no idea where she was going, she was just driving, trying to reach any destination that would distract her from herself.

Fifteen minutes later, she found herself parked outside a nightclub.

She remembered what she had told Alice days ago: “ Out where Alice? Bars? Clubs? Drinking all night and trying to pour my sadness and suffering into any girl's mouth? ”

The Irony of it all.

But now.... Now, it felt right. Now, it felt right to pour her sadness and suffering into someone's mouth. Now, was the right time to forget herself. To lose it all. Maybe it wasn't the best decision, maybe it was wrong, and maybe it is wrong. But it also felt right, it felt right to make someone else swallow her misery.

She got inside, and the neon lights welcomed her sight. The loud music, the smell of alcohol, sweat, and perfumes. Too many people. Normally, she'd turn around and go rot in her house, but it was already too late for that.

Half an hour passed, and she was two cocktails in. She stared at the ice in her glass when a dark–haired woman sat beside her at the bar.

“Hey.”

Rio looked at her for a second. “Hi.”

“On me,” the woman said as she pushed the cocktail closer to Rio.

“Thanks” Rio said with a chuckle.

“What are you doing her alone? Someone as beautiful as you...” The woman said as she tucked a strand of hair behind her ear, Rio only responded with a sidelong smile and took a sip from her glass.

“Are you enjoying your time?”

“Not much,” Rio said as she took the woman's hand off her cheek. “Not a fan of too much unnecessary touching.” She said then got up. “Excuse me,” and left.

Back to the dance floor, her eyes were wandering around. Then, she saw her—Agatha—at the back of the crowd with a woman younger than her by her side, too close to each other. Agatha's thumb stroking the exposed back of the woman.

The sight was agonizing.

Rio stood still in the middle of the dancing crowd, looking at Agatha. The smirk that appeared on Agatha's lips when the woman whispered something in her ear gave Rio goosebumps. The way Agatha's body swayed with the music, a drink in her hand while the other kept touching that blonde's back... Rio could only stare. She hadn't thought of Agatha as someone who went to clubs and enjoyed loud music and neon lights. But then again, what did she even know about Agatha? Nothing.

“You know nothing about her Rio.” She said, scolding herself.

As she kept looking at her, feeling like a creep, she imagined Agatha instead of that dark–haired woman at the bar, or herself by Agatha's side instead of that blonde woman. Then, as if she sensed it, Agatha found her eyes. From the distance. The lights went out for a brief second, then came back on. Agatha's eyes were still on her. The smirk on her face disappeared and was replaced by a shocked expression. She was stunned by seeing Rio, just as much as Rio was stunned by seeing her.

When the music stopped, Rio felt Agatha coming closer to her through the crowd. Agatha approached her.

“Rio,” She said, and that smirk returned to her lips.

“Agatha.”

They looked at each other, then both decided to get away from the noise. Rio was surprised that the blonde woman didn't follow Agatha, good.

They sat at the bar, and neither of them looked away, as if they were searching each other's eyes for answers.

“What are you doing here?” Rio asked, breaking the silence. Her tone was sharper than she intended.

“You gotta try LA clubs when you're here,” Agatha said with a smile.

“Yeah, you're right.” Rio said as she mirrored Agatha's smile.

Seconds of silence passed between them.

“What are you doing here...” Agatha paused, taking a sip from her glass. “By your own?”

“Blowing off some steam.”

“Mmm.” Agatha hummed as she looked at Rio, she looked tired, more than any other time Agatha had seen her before.

“Are you alright?” Agatha asked, trying to sound as casual as possible to avoid scaring Rio off, but there was real concern behind it.

Rio looked at Agatha's lips for a brief moment, then met her blue eyes. She stayed quiet for a moment.

“You don't have to answer that.” Agatha said, breaking the uncomfortable silence.

“No, it's okay. It's just some personal issues.... um, relationship issues.” Rio said as her eyes kept roaming over Agatha's face.

“So you're not single?” Agatha's tone sounded a bit disappointed.

“No, no, I am single.” She said as she looked at Agatha, the glittery mini black dress just above her thigh, the black high heels, her milky skin, the red lipstick, her silver earrings and necklace, her dark wavy hair, and her piercing blue eyes. She stared for a long time, almost lost herself in the woman's face and body.

She cleared her throat, when she looked back at Agatha. Agatha's smirk was deeper now, something wicked even.

“What about you?” Rio asked.

“What about me?”
